We are interested in the development of computing systems that interact with the physical world in an intelligent way. To investigate such systems, we focus on problems in robotics and activity recognition. We develop rich yet efficient techniques for perception and control in mobile robot navigation, map building, collaboration, and manipulation. We also develop state estimation and machine learning approaches for areas such as object recognition and tracking, human robot interaction, and human activity recognition.\\\\\\\"&amp;gt;\\\\n\\\\n&amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\"og:title\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\"Dieter Fox\\\\\\\"&amp;gt;\\\\n&amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\"og:site_title\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\"UW Robotics and State Estimation Lab\\\\\\\"&amp;gt;\\\\n&amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\"og:description\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\"The RSE-Lab was established in 2001. content=\\\\\\\"width=device-width, initial-scale=1\\\\\\\"&amp;gt;\\\\n\\\\n&amp;lt;title&amp;gt;Markus Grotz | UW Robotics and State Estimation Lab&amp;lt;/title&amp;gt;\\\\n\\\\n&amp;lt;link Grotz\\\\\\\"&amp;gt;\\\\n&amp;lt;meta name=\\\\\\\"description\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\"The RSE-Lab was established in 2001. We are interested in the development of computing systems that interact with the physical world in an intelligent way. To investigate such systems, we focus on problems in robotics and activity recognition. We develop rich yet efficient techniques for perception and control in mobile robot navigation, map building, collaboration, and manipulation. We also develop state estimation and machine learning approaches for areas such as object recognition and tracking, human robot interaction, and human activity recognition.\\\\\\\"&amp;gt;\\\\n\\\\n&amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\"og:title\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\"Markus Grotz\\\\\\\"&amp;gt;\\\\n&amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\"og:site_title\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\"UW Robotics and State Estimation Lab\\\\\\\"&amp;gt;\\\\n&amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\"og:description\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\"The RSE-Lab was established in 2001. We are interested in the development of computing systems that interact with the physical world in an intelligent way. To investigate such systems, we focus on problems in robotics and activity recognition. We develop rich yet efficient techniques for perception and control in mobile robot navigation, map building, collaboration, and manipulation. We also develop state estimation and machine learning approaches for areas such as object recognition and tracking, human robot interaction, and human activity recognition.\\\\\\\"&amp;gt;\\\\n&amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\"og:url\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\"https://laurenz-fx.github.io/lab-website-template\\\\\\\"&amp;gt;\\\\n&amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\"og:image\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\"/lab-website-template/images/share.jpg\\\\\\\"&amp;gt;\\\\n&amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\"og:locale\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\"en_US\\\\\\\"&amp;gt;\\\\n\\\\n&amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\"twitter:title\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\"Markus Grotz\\\\\\\"&amp;gt;\\\\n&amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\"twitter:description\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\"The RSE-Lab was established in 2001. We are interested in the development of computing systems that interact with the physical world in an intelligent way. To investigate such systems, we focus on problems in robotics and activity recognition. We develop rich yet efficient techniques for perception and control in mobile robot navigation, map building, collaboration, and manipulation. We also develop state estimation and machine learning approaches for areas such as object recognition and tracking, human robot interaction, and human activity recognition.\\\\\\\"&amp;gt;\\\\n&amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\"twitter:url\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\"https://laurenz-fx.github.io/lab-website-template\\\\\\\"&amp;gt;\\\\n&amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\"twitter:card\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\"summary_large_image\\\\\\\"&amp;gt;\\\\n&amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\"twitter:image\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\"/lab-website-template/images/share.jpg\\\\\\\"&amp;gt;\\\\n\\\\n\\\\n  &amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\"og:type\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\"website\\\\\\\"&amp;gt;\\\\n\\\\n\\\\n&amp;lt;script type=\\\\\\\"application/ld+json\\\\\\\"&amp;gt;\\\\n  {\\\\n    \\\\\\\"@context\\\\\\\": \\\\\\\"https://schema.org\\\\\\\",\\\\n    \\\\n      \\\\\\\"@type\\\\\\\": \\\\\\\"WebSite\\\\\\\",\\\\n    \\\\n    \\\\\\\"name\\\\\\\": \\\\\\\"Markus Grotz\\\\\\\",\\\\n    \\\\\\\"description\\\\\\\": \\\\\\\"The RSE-Lab was established in 2001. We are interested in the development of computing systems that interact with the physical world in an intelligent way. To investigate such systems, we focus on problems in robotics and activity recognition. We develop rich yet efficient techniques for perception and control in mobile robot navigation, map building, collaboration, and manipulation. We also develop state estimation and machine learning approaches for areas such as object recognition and tracking, human robot interaction, and human activity recognition.\\\\\\\",\\\\n We are interested in the development of computing systems that interact with the physical world in an intelligent way. To investigate such systems, we focus on problems in robotics and activity recognition. We develop rich yet efficient techniques for perception and control in mobile robot navigation, map building, collaboration, and manipulation. We also develop state estimation and machine learning approaches for areas such as object recognition and tracking, human robot interaction, and human activity recognition.\\\\\\\"&amp;gt;\\\\n\\\\n&amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\"og:title\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\"Dieter Fox\\\\\\\"&amp;gt;\\\\n&amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\"og:site_title\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\"UW Robotics and State Estimation Lab\\\\\\\"&amp;gt;\\\\n&amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\"og:description\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\"The RSE-Lab was established in 2001. We are interested in the development of computing systems that interact with the physical world in an intelligent way. To investigate such systems, we focus on problems in robotics and activity recognition. We develop rich yet efficient techniques for perception and control in mobile robot navigation, map building, collaboration, and manipulation. We also develop state estimation and machine learning approaches for areas such as object recognition and tracking, human robot interaction, and human activity recognition.\\\\\\\"&amp;gt;\\\\n\\\\n&amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\"og:title\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\"Markus Grotz\\\\\\\"&amp;gt;\\\\n&amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\"og:site_title\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\"UW Robotics and State Estimation Lab\\\\\\\"&amp;gt;\\\\n&amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\"og:description\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\"The RSE-Lab was established in 2001. Fox\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"&amp;amp;gt;\\\\\\\\n&amp;amp;lt;meta name=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"description\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"The RSE-Lab was established in 2001. We are interested in the development of computing systems that interact with the physical world in an intelligent way. To investigate such systems, we focus on problems in robotics and activity recognition. We develop rich yet efficient techniques for perception and control in mobile robot navigation, map building, collaboration, and manipulation. We also develop state estimation and machine learning approaches for areas such as object recognition and tracking, human robot interaction, and human activity recognition.\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"&amp;amp;gt;\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n&amp;amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"og:title\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"Dieter Fox\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"&amp;amp;gt;\\\\\\\\n&amp;amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"og:site_title\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"UW Robotics and State Estimation Lab\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"&amp;amp;gt;\\\\\\\\n&amp;amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"og:description\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"The RSE-Lab was established in 2001. We are interested in the development of computing systems that interact with the physical world in an intelligent way. To investigate such systems, we focus on problems in robotics and activity recognition. We develop rich yet efficient techniques for perception and control in mobile robot navigation, map building, collaboration, and manipulation. We also develop state estimation and machine learning approaches for areas such as object recognition and tracking, human robot interaction, and human activity recognition.\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"&amp;amp;gt;\\\\\\\\n&amp;amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"og:url\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"https://laurenz-fx.github.io/lab-website-template\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"&amp;amp;gt;\\\\\\\\n&amp;amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"og:image\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"/lab-website-template/images/share.jpg\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"&amp;amp;gt;\\\\\\\\n&amp;amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"og:locale\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"en_US\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"&amp;amp;gt;\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n&amp;amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"twitter:title\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"Dieter Fox\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"&amp;amp;gt;\\\\\\\\n&amp;amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"twitter:description\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"The RSE-Lab was established in 2001. We are interested in the development of computing systems that interact with the physical world in an intelligent way. To investigate such systems, we focus on problems in robotics and activity recognition. We develop rich yet efficient techniques for perception and control in mobile robot navigation, map building, collaboration, and manipulation. We also develop state estimation and machine learning approaches for areas such as object recognition and tracking, human robot interaction, and human activity recognition.\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"&amp;amp;gt;\\\\\\\\n&amp;amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"twitter:url\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"https://laurenz-fx.github.io/lab-website-template\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"&amp;amp;gt;\\\\\\\\n&amp;amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"twitter:card\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"summary_large_image\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"&amp;amp;gt;\\\\\\\\n&amp;amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"twitter:image\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"/lab-website-template/images/share.jpg\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"&amp;amp;gt;\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n  &amp;amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"og:type\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"website\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"&amp;amp;gt;\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n&amp;amp;lt;script type=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"application/ld+json\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"&amp;amp;gt;\\\\\\\\n  {\\\\\\\\n    \\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"@context\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\": \\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"https://schema.org\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\",\\\\\\\\n    \\\\\\\\n      \\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"@type\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\": \\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"WebSite\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\",\\\\\\\\n    \\\\\\\\n    \\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"name\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\": \\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"Dieter Fox\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\",\\\\\\\\n    \\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"description\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\": \\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"The RSE-Lab was established in 2001. We are interested in the development of computing systems that interact with the physical world in an intelligent way. Fox\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"&amp;amp;gt;\\\\\\\\n&amp;amp;lt;meta name=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"description\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"The RSE-Lab was established in 2001. We are interested in the development of computing systems that interact with the physical world in an intelligent way. To investigate such systems, we focus on problems in robotics and activity recognition. We develop rich yet efficient techniques for perception and control in mobile robot navigation, map building, collaboration, and manipulation. We also develop state estimation and machine learning approaches for areas such as object recognition and tracking, human robot interaction, and human activity recognition.\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"&amp;amp;gt;\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n&amp;amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"og:title\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"Dieter Fox\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"&amp;amp;gt;\\\\\\\\n&amp;amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"og:site_title\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"UW Robotics and State Estimation Lab\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"&amp;amp;gt;\\\\\\\\n&amp;amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"og:description\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"The RSE-Lab was established in 2001. We are interested in the development of computing systems that interact with the physical world in an intelligent way. To investigate such systems, we focus on problems in robotics and activity recognition. We develop rich yet efficient techniques for perception and control in mobile robot navigation, map building, collaboration, and manipulation. We also develop state estimation and machine learning approaches for areas such as object recognition and tracking, human robot interaction, and human activity recognition.\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"&amp;amp;gt;\\\\\\\\n&amp;amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"og:url\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"https://laurenz-fx.github.io/lab-website-template\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"&amp;amp;gt;\\\\\\\\n&amp;amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"og:image\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"/lab-website-template/images/share.jpg\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"&amp;amp;gt;\\\\\\\\n&amp;amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"og:locale\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"en_US\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"&amp;amp;gt;\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n&amp;amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"twitter:title\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"Dieter Fox\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"&amp;amp;gt;\\\\\\\\n&amp;amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"twitter:description\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"The RSE-Lab was established in 2001. We are interested in the development of computing systems that interact with the physical world in an intelligent way. To investigate such systems, we focus on problems in robotics and activity recognition. We develop rich yet efficient techniques for perception and control in mobile robot navigation, map building, collaboration, and manipulation. We also develop state estimation and machine learning approaches for areas such as object recognition and tracking, human robot interaction, and human activity recognition.\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"&amp;amp;gt;\\\\\\\\n&amp;amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"twitter:url\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"https://laurenz-fx.github.io/lab-website-template\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"&amp;amp;gt;\\\\\\\\n&amp;amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"twitter:card\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"summary_large_image\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"&amp;amp;gt;\\\\\\\\n&amp;amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"twitter:image\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"/lab-website-template/images/share.jpg\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"&amp;amp;gt;\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n  &amp;amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"og:type\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"website\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"&amp;amp;gt;\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n&amp;amp;lt;script type=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"application/ld+json\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"&amp;amp;gt;\\\\\\\\n  {\\\\\\\\n    \\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"@context\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\": \\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"https://schema.org\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\",\\\\\\\\n    \\\\\\\\n      \\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"@type\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\": \\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"WebSite\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\",\\\\\\\\n    \\\\\\\\n    \\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"name\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\": \\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"Dieter Fox\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\",\\\\\\\\n    \\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"description\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\": \\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"The RSE-Lab was established in 2001. content=\\\\\\\"width=device-width, initial-scale=1\\\\\\\"&amp;gt;\\\\n\\\\n&amp;lt;title&amp;gt;Helen Wang | UW Robotics and State Estimation Lab&amp;lt;/title&amp;gt;\\\\n\\\\n&amp;lt;link rel=\\\\\\\"icon\\\\\\\" href=\\\\\\\"/lab-website-template/images/icon.png\\\\\\\"&amp;gt;\\\\n\\\\n&amp;lt;meta name=\\\\\\\"title\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\"Helen Wang\\\\\\\"&amp;gt;\\\\n&amp;lt;meta name=\\\\\\\"description\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\"The RSE-Lab was established in 2001. We are interested in the development of computing systems that interact with the physical world in an intelligent way. To investigate such systems, we focus on problems in robotics and activity recognition. We develop rich yet efficient techniques for perception and control in mobile robot navigation, map building, collaboration, and manipulation. We also develop state estimation and machine learning approaches for areas such as object recognition and tracking, human robot interaction, and human activity recognition.\\\\\\\"&amp;gt;\\\\n\\\\n&amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\"og:title\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\"Helen Wang\\\\\\\"&amp;gt;\\\\n&amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\"og:site_title\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\"UW Robotics and State Estimation Lab\\\\\\\"&amp;gt;\\\\n&amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\"og:description\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\"The RSE-Lab was established in 2001. We are interested in the development of computing systems that interact with the physical world in an intelligent way. To investigate such systems, we focus on problems in robotics and activity recognition. We develop rich yet efficient techniques for perception and control in mobile robot navigation, map building, collaboration, and manipulation. We also develop state estimation and machine learning approaches for areas such as object recognition and tracking, human robot interaction, and human activity recognition.\\\\\\\"&amp;gt;\\\\n&amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\"og:url\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\"https://laurenz-fx.github.io/lab-website-template\\\\\\\"&amp;gt;\\\\n&amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\"og:image\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\"/lab-website-template/images/share.jpg\\\\\\\"&amp;gt;\\\\n&amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\"og:locale\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\"en_US\\\\\\\"&amp;gt;\\\\n\\\\n&amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\"twitter:title\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\"Helen Wang\\\\\\\"&amp;gt;\\\\n&amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\"twitter:description\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\"The RSE-Lab was established in 2001. We are interested in the development of computing systems that interact with the physical world in an intelligent way. To investigate such systems, we focus on problems in robotics and activity recognition. We develop rich yet efficient techniques for perception and control in mobile robot navigation, map building, collaboration, and manipulation. We also develop state estimation and machine learning approaches for areas such as object recognition and tracking, human robot interaction, and human activity recognition.\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"&amp;amp;gt;\\\\\\\\n\\\\\\\\n&amp;amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"og:title\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"Markus Grotz\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"&amp;amp;gt;\\\\\\\\n&amp;amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"og:site_title\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"UW Robotics and State Estimation Lab\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"&amp;amp;gt;\\\\\\\\n&amp;amp;lt;meta property=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"og:description\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\" content=\\\\\\\\\\\\\\\"The RSE-Lab was established in 2001.
